It is necessary for me to say the quality of the benefits and harms of that cautery, and in what combination it is forbidden to use cauterization.
Therefore I say that the discourse on the quality of the benefits and harms of cautery is lengthy and verbose, subtle with knowledge, and hidden secrets; and many wise people have spoken about it, and they disagree on many points, and I can only cover a small part of their speeches, for fear of being too long.
And so I say that cautery benefits all universal compositions, whether with or without matter, with two exceptions: the two compositions which are dry and without matter.
In a dry and thin constitution, the body becomes unbalanced; for some say that cautery is beneficial for this condition, while others say the contrary, that cautery is not appropriate for a disease that is caused by heat and dryness, since the nature of fire is also hot and dry. It would be inappropriate to try to heal a dry and thin condition with something that is also hot and dry.
And those who say the contrary argue that cautery is beneficial for any dry and thin disease that occurs in the human body, because when compared to the nature of fire, the human body is much colder.
And I say from experience, that I have tried this several times and discovered that it is true.
However, it is not appropriate for someone who has already studied and practiced cautery in the previous chapter to rush into this without considering the individual constitution of each person, the different types of illnesses they may have, their causes and symptoms, and the right time to use cautery as a treatment.
But in other constitutions, there is no reason to be afraid, especially in cases of cold and wet illnesses, for all doctors agree on this point and do not hesitate to use cautery as a treatment for such conditions.
And know, my child, that the secret to curing with cautery using fire and its benefits lies in using a burning medicine, for fire is simple and its action only affects the body part that is being cauterized, without harming other connected parts more than slightly.
But the action of a burning medicine also reaches the neighboring members and can quickly bring to the affected area a difficult-to-heal illness or make it worse.
But fire, due to its exalted nature and inherent goodness, does not cause harm in this way. This is known through experience and long study of the art, and for that reason I will not prolong my explanation. If it were not for the fact that it is not appropriate to reveal secret knowledge in this public place, I would explain with philosophical arguments the qualities of fire's operation in the body and its ability to expel illnesses, so that you may understand better.
And know, my child, that some people do not consider the right time to perform cautery and mistakenly choose the beginning of spring as the best time.
I say that cautery is appropriate in any season, because the harm caused by the accidental timing is outweighed by the benefits of cauterization, especially if it is used to alleviate severe and persistent pain that cannot afford to wait, for fear of causing greater harm than the slight damage caused by performing cautery at an inconvenient time.
And this is not the case in your situation, my child, for only the ignorant masses and foolish doctors would argue that a disease should never be treated with cautery. The right time to use cautery depends on the specific condition being treated.
And the reason for this is not as they think, for cautery is simply a substitute for medicine that alters the constitution and dries up the excess moisture that causes pain.
However, cautery is often used in place of medicine due to its effectiveness and the power and greatness of its action.
It is possible that the illness may return at some point in the future, depending on the individual's constitution and the location of the illness, as well as its strength and any excess moisture present in their body, and anything they have consumed that contributes to the illness. However, if cautery is administered for a subtle illness affecting a member with little excess moisture or fluid, it is possible that the pain will not return, although it may recur on a smaller scale.
And the common saying is that cautery is the last resort of medicine, and this is true, but not in the way I think you understand it. For I do not believe that cauterization is the only cure for an illness, nor do I think it is superior to other forms of treatment.
On the contrary, the meaning of the saying that cautery is the last resort of medicine is simply that when other methods of treatment have been tried and have failed to bring relief, cauterization may be administered as a final attempt to cure the illness. And so from this it is clear that the saying "cautery is the last resort of medicine" does not mean what the ignorant masses and foolish doctors think it means.
The ancients believed that cautery with gold was better than cautery with iron, and they did not believe this without reason, for gold is equal in status and has a more noble substance.
The ancients believed that the location of cautery did not matter, but this is not entirely true, for I have found through experience that it does make a difference in some cases. Cauterization with gold is indeed better and more effective than iron, as they claimed. However, when using fire to cauterize with gold, one must be careful to use the right amount of heat, for too much can cause the gold to melt and become damaged, making it unusable.
And so cautery is performed with iron by applying it gently and precisely in order to achieve the desired result.
I have now organized this chapter on cautery in a logical manner, dividing it into sections from the head to the feet, in order to make it easier for you to find what you need.
The first chapter.
This cauterization treats the wetness and cold of the service accident, which has two causes: first, an excess of moisture that can cause headaches, migraines, ear infections, and excessive sleep, toothaches, and dizziness, as well as general illness caused by cold. It is also used to treat paralysis, seizures, apoplexy, and similar conditions. [
The method of this cauterization is as follows: first, the patient must be evacuated with a laxative medicine to cleanse the head and scalp for three or four nights, depending on the severity of their condition, their age, and their lifestyle. This will help to prepare the area for cauterization and ensure that any impurities are removed from the body.
And then you should instruct the patient to shave their head with a razor, and have them lean back on a slanted bench with their feet raised and placed on a stool. This will help to improve blood flow to the head and make it easier to perform the cauterization. It is important to ensure that the patient is comfortable and relaxed throughout the procedure, as this can help to reduce anxiety and promote healing.
And then you should place the edge of your palm on the bridge of the patient's nose, between their eyes. This is a common position for cauterization of the head and scalp, as it allows for easy access to the affected area while also providing support and stability for the patient. However, if the desired location for cauterization has been reached, mark that spot with a pen or other marker. Then, ignite the olive-shaped cautery tool, which has the following form:
And then place the olive-shaped cautery tool over the marked location on the patient's head, applying gentle downward pressure so that the skin is slowly constricted. As you do this, rotate the tool slowly to ensure even application of heat and prevent burning or other complications.
And then gently lift your hand away and check the location of the cauterization. If you see that any amount of skull has been exposed, such as the size of a grain of barley, then raise your hand and apply more pressure with the cautery tool until you can see the bone clearly, as I have described.
And then take a small amount of salt and dissolve it over the cauterized area, leaving it in place for three days. This will help to promote healing and prevent infection.
And then place a piece of clean, dry cloth over the wound and leave it in place until the scab from the cauterization has been completely destroyed by the heat. This will help to protect the wound from infection and promote healing. And then treat the wound with a tetrafarmed ointment until it is healed. This will help to soothe any pain or discomfort and promote healing, ensuring the best possible outcome for the patient.
And it has been said that when the wound remains open for a longer period of time, it heals better and is more beneficial, as it allows for greater exposure to air and improved healing. However, this is not always the case, and in some situations, it may be necessary to close the wound more quickly to prevent infection or other complications.
And some have said that the coccyx, or tailbone, should be cauterized all the way down to the bone, and that the cautery tool should be left in place until it becomes attached to a portion of the bone. This is a more extreme form of cauterization that is typically reserved for severe or chronic conditions that have not responded to other forms of treatment.
And then the area that has become attached to the bone should be shaved and treated. This may involve removing any remaining cautery tool or other foreign material, as well as cleaning and dressing the wound to promote healing and prevent infection.
And others have said that the cautery tool should be applied to the very end, so that it penetrates deeply into the bone and causes significant damage. This is known as alphecatia, and it is a more extreme form of cauterization that is typically reserved for severe or chronic conditions that have not responded to other forms of treatment. And they consider that vapors from the head escape from that place.
And keep the wound open for a long time, and let it be healed until it is solidified.
But I do not advise the use of these two types of cautery in all cases, but only in certain ones and according to my judgment; and it is better for you, while you are healthy, to leave it alone; because the head is uncovered by a solution of its continuity, just as we have testified in other members, and especially when the patient's head is of a hot nature.
And the first type of cautery is safer and better in my opinion; and with that one, do the work while being safe.
Second chapter.
On cauterization of the head.
When chronic and long-lasting pain occurs throughout the head of a patient and it has persisted for a long time, and various treatments such as cuppings, coctions, cataplasms, emplasters, lotions, potions, pills, and similar remedies have been used, and especially if the patient has already been cauterized with one cautery but it has not helped with any of those causes, then consider that if the patient's head is of a strong constitution in its nature and is not hot, and a great cold is found, then cauterize that area again with another cautery, but only slightly. And cauterize the area above the patient's ear with a cautery while the vein is still open. Incise the vein and expose the bone to the extent that we have determined, and then cauterize the area behind the patient's head at the location called "vas", which is where a cupping glass is applied. And move your hand gently in this process, without exposing the bone, because the patient will experience a great deal of pain that is different from the pain caused by other cauteries on the head.
And I say that this cautery should be used in its place, because it is necessary that the cautery used to cauterize the corners of the head and the occiput is more subtle than the one used to cauterize the middle of the head; and this is the method for doing so.
Third chapter.
On cauterization of new migraines.
When pain occurs in a part of the head, either as a sudden pain or a continuous pain extending to the eye, then evacuate the head with purgative medicines and administer another treatment, which I have mentioned for other illnesses; and if that does not work, then cauterization is necessary in two ways: either with a burning and acrid medicine or with iron.
But cauterization with a burning medicine is done by taking a piece of aloe wood and charring it, and then applying the hot ends to both ends of the area to be cauterized. And then make an incision in the area of pain in the temple with a sharp lancet until you reach the bone and it is hidden from view.
And then apply pressure to the area with a piece of cloth to reduce constriction and leave it for three hours; and then remove the aloe wood and let the wound remain open for two or three days, and then place a compress soaked in warm water over the area until the bone is healed.
And then treat the area with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, do so with some burning medicines which I have written about in the second treatise on burning medicines.
But cauterization with iron is done in this way: heat the iron for cautery, and it should be shaped as follows:
and it is called "clavis claviculae", because its shape resembles a key with a slight curvature in the middle.
And then place the iron on the area of pain and hold it there firmly so that it does not slip, while rotating it slowly at a moderate speed.
And if the amount of tissue that is burnt by the tip of the iron reaches the bone, lift your hand slightly so that the artery below is not burnt and there is no bleeding.
And then apply a compress soaked in salt water to the area and leave it for three days; and then place a compress soaked in warm water over the wound, and treat it with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize with the tip of a knife as in cautery, and be careful not to cut an artery in this new type of migraine.
Fourth chapter.
On cauterization of old migraines.
When you treat migraines with what we have said in the previous treatment, and what we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and it is not helpful, and sometimes due to the severity of the illness, what we have said about the first cautery with medicine or with fire is not sufficient, then it is necessary to heat the knife-shaped cautery until it turns white, because this means that you should place it on the area of pain with a line as long as your finger, or even longer; and then place your hand firmly over it and press down so that you can cut through the artery and reach the bone.
However, it is important for you to be careful not to damage the jaw joint due to chewing, and not to burn the tendons or nerves that move it, and not to cause spasms.
And regarding the precautions and caution to be taken in case of bleeding from the cut artery, there is fear because cutting it is dangerous, especially for those who are not knowledgeable about what they are doing and lack experience; and so leave the operation to a more experienced practitioner at the beginning.
And I will come back with a reminder of the treatment for bleeding from an artery, according to its type, in its appropriate place in this book.
And if you see that this type of cautery is not sufficient for this illness and the patient's body can tolerate it, then cauterize the area in the middle of the head as we have described, and heal the wound until it is fully healed.
And if you wish, use the cautery that we described in the chapter on stretching an artery with two knives, as this is better and more effective.
Fifth chapter.
On cauterization of ear pain.
When there is ear pain due to cold and it is treated with purgative medicines and other treatments that I have mentioned, but the pain does not go away, then heat the needle-shaped cautery, which is called "puncta". The shape of this cautery is as follows: [image of a needle-shaped cautery].
And then heat the needle-shaped cautery and move it around the entire ear in a circular motion, or in the circumference of each part if the pain is in one specific area. Guide the needle-shaped cautery along the ridge of the ear, a little at a time, after marking the area with a probe.
And if you use a cautery with ten points on the entire ear, and place it there firmly so that it does not slip, while rotating it slowly at a moderate speed. After cauterization, apply a compress soaked in salt water to each of the burnt areas, and leave them for three days. And then place a compress soaked in warm water over the wound, and treat it with an ointment until it is healed.
Sixth chapter.
Of the cauterization of swelling.
Swelling, which is cured and cauterization of which is only of the kinds that come through vein-flecking, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid cauterization of the kind that occurs through drying or spasm of the nerve.
When you cure that kind of swelling with jerras and capipurgi and guarguarismes, and you don't find the cure effective, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: the first at the tip of the ear, the second a little below its temperature, and the third at the junction of two labia.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the affected area, because softening will not occur in the part that appears sick.
And the method of cauterization is that you cauterize with the cautery on the right side of the highest point of the ear, rising slightly above the top of the head, and in temperature another, the length of which should be according to the length of the finger, and then place your hand with the heated cautery until it has burned the amount corresponding to the thickness of the swelling.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is the specialty of the cutler, the shape of which is in front of the table. However, it is more subtle that what you see, and it is necessary for the knife to be slightly less thick than superfluous thickness.
Then heal the area with what is prepared beforehand until it is healed.
Capital VII.
Of the cauterization of old apoplexy.

And the method of cauterization is done as previously stated.
And it has already been cauterized on the mouth of the stomach, and further back; then let it be healed with what is prepared beforehand.

Of the cauterization for forgetfulness made through flame.

Of the cauterization for paralysis and softening of the entire body.

Capital X.
Of the cauterization for epilepsy.
An epileptic should not be cauterized unless the epilepsy is through vein-flecking (blood vessels).
And therefore, it is necessary to cleanse the brain of the patient at the beginning with jerras (enemas) and with other remedies that have been mentioned in the division when the patient's illness is severe and they are intolerant to exceptional medical treatments.
And if it is a child who does not tolerate medications, then administer laxatives and chewing remedies for several days beforehand, along with improvement of their diet.
And then shave the patient's head and cauterize them in the middle of the head with a heated cautery using the previous method, and on the back of their neck, and on each corner of their head. And if the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize them with heated cauteries as I have said, having paralysis and softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and back.
And let it be olive-shaped as previously described.
But if the patient is a child, then place a subtle cautery in this manner. (Note: the text does not provide further information about "this manner")
Capital XI.
Of the cauterization for melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted wetness and thick flame, then cauterize them with the heated cauteries that I mentioned in the case of paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is superfluity inclined towards melancholy and the patient's body is wet, then give them to drink something that cleanses their brain according to what has been previously stated in the division (section).
And approach the patient's head, and place a well-made touret (an instrument used to calm restless patients) on their forehead, and then place it in the middle of their head.
And let the patient be sixty years old and held firmly from all sides.
Then apply a liniment; and it is preferable to use an antidote made from sheep's wool. And heat that (liniment) over the fire for a moderate warmth, which will relieve the suffering when it is applied to the affected area. Then apply that (liniment) in the middle of their forehead on the "touret," and let it remain until they are refreshed.
And do this to the patient once a week, along with other beneficial treatments until they are healed; or if you prefer, cauterize the affected area with small points as needed, but make sure your hand is equipped with a cautery tool in this manner: This is a type of cautery that moistens the brain with evenness.
Then place a piece of linen soaked in a mixture of bread or wool grease.
Chapter 12.
Chapter 12: On cauterization of water that descends to the joint.
When you have determined the onset of water in the joint by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin (the treatment) and give the patient to drink something that will purify their head, and keep them away from all moisture.
And have them sweat in a bath for several days.
And order the patient to shave their head, and cauterize that area in the middle of their head with a cautery tool; and furthermore, cauterize that area with two cauteries on both temples if it is the beginning of water descending into two joints, or on one temple if it is the beginning of water in one joint.
Cut with a cautery tool all the veins and arteries that are located below the temples; and let the cauteries be in that line at the width of the temples.
And be careful not to cause bleeding when cauterizing; and if you see any bleeding, stop it with some medicine that is within your means.
And bring with you skill in the extraction of arteries and in the incision of those (blood vessels) and caution regarding bleeding.
And sometimes it is necessary to cauterize in the back of the neck, between two bones, with two well-made cauteries.
Chapter 13.
Chapter 13: On cauterization of old tears (eye styes).
When the tears of the eyes have become old and hardened due to veins and arteries in the visible part of the head outside and it is confirmed that this is a superfluous, fleck-like accumulation, then cauterize with a cautery tool as described in the chapter on water descending into the joints. Cauterize in the middle of the forehead, between two temples, and between two bones in the back of the neck with two well-made cauteries each time. And if necessary, also cauterize in the corner of the eye, on the outside edge of the eyebrow, with a small cautery tool.
Chapter 14.
Chapter 14: On cauterization of foul odor of the nose.
When you treat that with what we have mentioned in the division and your treatment does not improve, then prepare (a remedy) and give the patient to drink the juice of cochineal for three nights; and furthermore, approach the patient's head and cauterize it with a medium-sized olive-shaped cautery tool. And furthermore, cauterize that with a carnation-shaped cautery tool with two well-made cauteries just below the eyebrows, on both sides of the hairline.

Chapter 53.
On the cauterization of wounds and similar ones.
Many wounds are often found in the lower parts of a sick person's foot, which is called a "clau," and it is a serious, wide opening that exposes the inside of the foot; and cauterization in such cases can be done in two ways: either with fire or with hot water.

This involves taking a small piece of iron, copper, or a vulture's beak, and placing it over the ulcer. Then, pour a small amount of hot water over the piece, keeping your hand steady while rotating it completely around the ulcer. Make sure that the edge of the piece is pressed against the root of the ulcer, creating a path for the hot water to enter. Have the patient endure the burning sensation of the hot water for an hour, and then remove the cautery, as this will help draw out the root cause from the ulcer.
And do the same with all others, until they are all treated in this way on their bodies.

Chapter 56.
On the cauterization of bleeding caused by a ruptured blood vessel through incision.
Often, bleeding occurs from a wound on the surface of the body, or from an incision made during surgery to treat abscesses or cauterize a limb, and it can be difficult to stop this type of bleeding.
Therefore, when this happens, place your hand over the opening of the blood vessel and apply pressure with your finger until the bleeding stops completely and does not start again.
Then place the hot, olive-shaped cauteries over the area and blow on them until they become very hot.
Take one or more of the hot cauteries and place them on the wound, pressing firmly until the bleeding stops completely and the wound is sealed.
If blood continues to flow from the wound after you have applied and removed the hot cautery, then take another cautery that has been prepared in the fire and repeat the process until the bleeding stops completely.
Be careful not to burn the nerves in that area and avoid causing further harm or injury to the patient.
And you should know that when blood flows from an artery, it is not possible to stop the bleeding using pressure alone, especially if the artery is large. There are four ways to stop the bleeding: with cautery as described earlier, through extraction if possible, because if the ends of the severed artery are burned and sealed, the bleeding will stop; by tying it off with thread or ligament to compress the area; or by applying medicines that constrict blood vessels. These medicines should be strengthened with a cushion and proper compression.
But those who apply restriction with ligatures or tight bandages, using heating pads or similar methods, should be cautious and not rush the process.
But if this happens when a doctor is not present and no medicine is available, then place your finger over the opening of the vein as described earlier, and apply firm pressure to stop the bleeding until the wound has healed sufficiently. Do not press on the artery or cause further damage. If possible, sprinkle cold water on the area around the artery to cool it down and thicken the blood, and consider using cautery or other medical treatments if necessary.

Chapter two.

Chapter 13.

Of incision of a nail and fleshy eminence of the tear gland.

Of the cure for flesh grown inside the nose.
When diverse kinds of flesh have grown inside the nose, which are caused by something that resembles a scorpion with heavy stings or a fleshy polyp, and this illness is called "polipus" because it resembles such a thing. And then place it inside the nose, close to the incision with vinegar or wine. If the nose becomes runny and the patient expels humidity into the palate, then you know that they are cured.

But if the abscess is soft to the touch and not dark in color, and it is possible to incise all of it, then evacuate the patient and incise the abscess without fear, and cure the location with a drying and constricting substance until it heals.

Chapter 30.
On the extraction of teeth.
It is necessary that you treat the tooth for its pain with all care and caution during its extraction, because there is no reason to rush the procedure when extracting it, since it is a subtle substance that must be carefully extracted.
But when the patient is forced to undergo tooth extraction, you must be certain which tooth is causing the pain, because often the pain can deceive the patient and they think it's in a healthy tooth, and then you extract that one but the pain doesn't stop until the diseased and painful tooth has been extracted. We have seen this happen in barbers' operations.
Therefore, how do you determine which tooth is causing the pain? Well, you should make an incision in the gum around the tooth using a spatula with some power (i.e., a medicinal substance), until it has dissolved the connection between the tooth and the gum from all sides. Then, use those same tweezers or fine forceps to gently and gradually pull on the tooth until you extract it.
And then, place forceps with large and strong tongs in the patient's mouth for good grip or firm control, and hold their head between your knees to keep them still, and extract the tooth carefully and steadily without breaking it or causing the patient more pain.
And so, if it is not loose already, take one of those instruments and place it under the tooth from all sides with ease and apply gentle force to lift it out, just as you would at the beginning of the extraction.
But if the tooth is cracked or corroded, then you must wrap a cloth around the crack and tighten it with a thin thread so that it does not break when you apply force to extract it using the tongs.
It is necessary to work carefully with the incision around the entire gum and be very careful not to break the tooth while tightening it. Leave it partially extracted, and then turn your attention back to the patient, who may become more mischievous than the initial pain.
And beware that you do not make the same mistakes as some ignorant barbers in their haste and recklessness during tooth extraction, for many times they do not use what we have recommended, causing great harm to the patient, leading to more serious conditions that are difficult to cure, and damaging the gums or extracting the tooth along with some bones from the jaw, as we have often witnessed.
And then, after extracting the tooth, rinse out the patient's mouth with wine vinegar or wine and salt to clean it.
And if bleeding persists after that, as it often does, then sprinkle some powdered yarrow on the wound and repeat this procedure until the bleeding stops. If it doesn't stop, cauterize the area with a hot iron.
The shape of the forceps and fine tongs used to extract the tooth should have a long handle, a short shank, and be thick, so that they are not bent when you use them for extraction.
And they should have handles that are thick enough so that when you squeeze them, they do not bend, and the shanks should be short.
And they should be made of Indian steel, with right-angled shanks, and the ends of those shanks should have teeth that fit into one another to increase the force of the grip. Sometimes the shape of the ends may resemble a stork's beak (in Latin, "ciconia" means "stork"), which is very strong.

Chapter 32.
On the care of prominent teeth over others.
When teeth protrude unnaturally, particularly in women and more so in young girls, it is necessary to consider: if the tooth does not touch another tooth and there is no possibility of a fracture or gap between them, then you should extract that tooth; but do not allow it to be adjacent to another tooth. And make sure your grinding is gradual so that you grind down the tooth over several days due to its hardness, and do not damage other teeth in the process. (Note: "Comauguda" may be derived from the Latin term for damaging or wearing away something.)

And it should be made entirely of Indian iron and have many small points like a file with needles, which can be used to carefully grind down the tooth little by little over several days without damaging other teeth or causing injury. And finally, smooth down the tooth and remove any rough edges with these other razors.
And if part of the tooth is fractured and irritating the tongue, then it is necessary to grind down that area until its roughness has been removed and covered, and filled in so that the tongue does not become damaged or speech impaired.
Chapter 33.
On restoring damaged teeth with gold or silver filings.
When damage occurs to the front teeth due to concussion or loss from percussion or extraction, and the patient is unable to chew properly, and you have treated it with styptic medications without success, then in order to prevent further harm, use gold filings instead of silver, because silver turns green and may need to be replaced after a few days, while gold never changes.
And the bile should be of such fineness and thickness according to the quantity that can enter between the teeth; and the method of rection is to take the bile and place twice as much of it between two healthy teeth, and then curve it with two twists of the bile between two bad teeth, or if there is one or many, until the cloth reaches the healthy tooth on the other side. And then repeat the treatment on the same area that you began with, and strengthen your hand with ease and skill so that it is not harmful.
And let the strip of cloth that you use to strengthen the bile be of the right size so that it does not escape from between the teeth.
And then cut off the excess bile with forceps or tweezers and add it to each location with caution, and turn and hide those between the healthy tooth and the bad tooth, so that it does not cause injury to the tongue. And then leave it as tight as a Roman.
But if it becomes loose or broken, strengthen it again with more bile in the same manner for its entire duration.

Chapter 34.
Of the incision of the ligament that is on the tongue and prevents speech.
This ligament that is seen below the tongue can sometimes be congenital or natural at birth, or it can be acquired and occur due to an injury that has already healed.
And the operation for this is to have the patient open their mouth with your head inside, and then lift their tongue and make an incision in the ligament nerve according to its width so that the tongue is freed from its restriction.
But if there is any hardness or thickening in that area, and it has formed due to the healing of an injury, then you should apply a probe and cut through it according to its width so that you have made an incision in the ligament and the thickening has been released.
And be careful to not make a fissure in the skin and instead cut only through the ligament, ensuring that there is no flow of blood.
And then the wound from the incision should be washed with water, vinegar, or warm water, and a ligature should be placed below the tongue, which is a device that holds the patient's tongue down to prevent it from healing improperly again.
But if there is a flow of blood, place a piece of vitriol trissat on the location, but if the bleeding persists, then cauterize the area with a lance-shaped cautery that is appropriate for this purpose. And then continue with other treatments for any additional causes until it is healed.
Chapter 35.
Of extracting a ranula from beneath the tongue.
Sometimes, a small abscess can form beneath the tongue that resembles a ranula and prevents it from performing its natural functions, and it can quickly grow to fill the entire mouth.
And the operation for this is to have the patient open their mouth wide in front of the sun and observe the abscess.
And if you see that it is dark or black in color and hard, and the patient cannot feel it, then do not touch it because it is dead tissue.
And if it has turned white and is moist, then place a probe into it and make an incision around the entire area with a sharp spatula, cutting through all of the affected tissue; and if bleeding occurs during your procedure, then apply a piece of vitriol trissat to stop it.
And then continue your work until it has been completely drained, and wash the area with a mixture of vinegar and salt, and treat any remaining issues until it is healed.
Chapter 36.
Of extracting an abscess from both ears, and of those located in the throat, and of other abscesses.
When a goiter occurs in the throat, it is caused by glands that are enlarged and resemble cotton, which can sometimes protrude outside of the body and are called "two ears." But if it is white in color, round, and the tissue is thin, then that is what needs to be incised.
And the operation for this is to first consider whether the abscess has completely subsided on its own or if it has decreased in size before proceeding with surgery. I have treated a woman with an abscess that was located in her groin and tended to be dark colored with little sensation, who had already closed the area and the woman was breathing with difficulty, and she had been prohibited from eating and drinking water, and she would have died if it had lasted for another day or two.
And the abscess had grown so much that it had taken two months to burst through two openings.
Therefore I proceeded fistulously and inserted my finger into one of the openings, and pulled out a large portion from it, and then I incised the other part that was not open, and forced open its mouth, and compressed its tongue, and then I inserted the instrument into the abscess.

And I did not stop incising the abscess many times for a long time, and an ulcer formed in place of it, which continued to grow over time.
Therefore I put medicine in it and cauterized the woman's groin, and that is all for now. And then I left and did not know what God did with her afterwards.

Chapter 40.
In which we summarize the discussion on abscesses and their treatment.
Abscesses are of many types and forms, as remembered from the descriptions in this book, each with their own characteristics.
Abscesses are differentiated by the way they open and their shape in two ways: one based on the type of abscess itself, and another based on the underlying cause of the accumulation of fluid or pus. [*](Note: The text seems to be referring to two types of abscesses, those that open and drain naturally through a predetermined pathway (perforatio propria) and those that do not have a natural opening and require surgical intervention (perforatio impropria). Additionally, the text suggests that the shape and form of the abscess are influenced by the underlying cause of the accumulation of fluid or pus.)*
And the second way is based on the location of the abscess in the body, as an abscess in the head is different from one in the buttocks, and an abscess in a fleshy area is different from one in a joint; and each of them requires its own surgical treatment. [*](Note: The text suggests that the location of the abscess influences its form and shape, and as such, the surgical approach to treating it must be tailored to the specific location of the abscess in the body.)*[*](The word "accident" is used here in a medical sense, meaning "occurrence".)*
And there are some abscesses that should not be opened until the pus is fully mature or the healing process has been completed. [*](Note: The text suggests that some abscesses may heal without surgical intervention, and that waiting for maturation of the pus can lead to a more successful outcome.)*
And there are other abscesses that should be opened immediately when they become hard and do not mature according to their normal course, such as those near joints, because an abscess located near a joint will continue to grow until it affects the surrounding ligaments or nerves, causing contraction of the affected member. Or if it is near a major organ, waiting for maturation can lead to damage to that organ. Or if it is in the buttocks, then drainage should be performed even if it is not mature, so as to prevent infection from spreading to deeper tissues and causing fistula or other complications. And it is important to know the correct time for opening the abscess, which is when it has matured.
And know that it is mature when there is a decrease in pain and fever, along with reduced redness and swelling, decreased tenderness, and the appearance of softening or thinning of the skin over the abscess. *(*Note: The text suggests that signs of maturation include both systemic and local symptoms.)*
And it is important to ensure that the incision is made in a location below the abscess, allowing the pus to drain freely and not accumulate again. *(*Note: The text suggests that the incision should be made in a dependent position relative to the abscess to facilitate complete drainage of the pus.)*
And the incision should always be made along the length of the skin or body, especially for abscesses located in areas such as the armpits, groin, and wrist, where there are tendons and blood vessels; and in general, avoid making incisions on joints or other areas that may impair mobility.
But if the abscess is located in a fleshy area, it is better to wait until the maturation process has been completed before making an incision, as described earlier, because making an incision too early can cause the pus and debris to spread further, leading to increased pain, swelling, and risk of infection. *(*Note: The text suggests waiting for complete maturation of the abscess in fleshy areas to avoid complications.)*
But some abscesses require immediate surgical intervention due to their location or the severity of symptoms, regardless of the maturation process. *(*Note: The text suggests that certain circumstances may necessitate urgent surgical intervention, even if the abscess has not fully matured.)*
And it is important to make the incision proportional to the size of the abscess, with a small incision for smaller abscesses and larger, more extensive incisions for larger abscesses. *(*Note: The text suggests that the size of the incision should be appropriate for the size of the abscess to ensure adequate drainage and minimize risk of complications.)*[*](The word "seccios" is used here in a medical sense, meaning "sections" or "incisions", referring to the surgical approach to opening the abscess for proper drainage.)*
And other abscesses require a different surgical approach, such as making the incision in a concave shape and then closing it with sutures once the pus has drained completely, which is often necessary for abscesses located in areas with thin skin or at risk of herniation. *(*Note: The text suggests that some abscesses may require more complex surgical techniques to ensure proper healing.)*[*](The word "codena" is used here in a medical sense, meaning "incision", and "encidida" refers to the closure of the incision with sutures once the pus has drained completely. This technique is often necessary for abscesses located in areas with thin skin or at risk of herniation.)*
And some abscesses are opened with a three-sided incision or in the shape of a myrtle leaf, which is often necessary for abscesses located in areas with a high risk of infection or those requiring more extensive drainage. *(*Note: The text suggests that some abscesses may require more complex surgical techniques to ensure proper healing and minimize the risk of complications.)*[*](The word "insciditz" is used here in a medical sense, meaning "incised", referring to the surgical opening of the abscess. The term "fuelha de mirtra" refers to the myrtle leaf shape that may be used for incisions in certain locations or types of abscesses.)*[*](The word "angonars" is a medical term used to describe anatomical areas where herniation may occur, such as the groin or armpit. The text suggests that some abscesses located in these areas may require more complex surgical techniques for proper healing and minimizing risk of complications.)*

Chapter 41.
Chapter 41: On the incision of abscesses that appear on the back of the head.
On the back of the head, there are small abscesses that take on the form of nodes and contain tunics that correspond to their formation; and their types are many.
And from some of them come pus, and from others comes moisture similar to lime. And for those that contain moisture similar to dust and resemble them; and for those that are stony and hard.

Once the moisture has been drained, you should scrape away the surrounding tissue that contained the pus or other infectious material, making sure to remove all of it completely. Then, if necessary, repeat the application of Egyptian ointment to the cotton and apply it to the wound a second and third time, until you are confident that all remaining tissue has been dissolved. After that, treat the wound with a general salve until it is healed.

On the incision of types of nodules.
There are many species of nodes and I have already mentioned all their species in the division (classification).
And it is necessary for me to repeat the difference between a node and an abscess, as there may be doubt.
And so I say that with an abscess there is heat and fever and intense pain until the boiling of the excess fluid has subsided; and it is a complete putrefaction that then stops the fever, pain, and heat.
The main symptom is not heat or fever or pain, but rather that hiccup-like sensation in the region of the lung, which is specifically located in its own sac.
And it depends on the color of the body (of the hiccup), and its initial stage is like a sneeze, and it occurs either more or less severely. It comes in two forms: one is caused by thick humors and contains moisture, and the humors are speckled, as I said in my division.
Therefore, when you come to the cure for hiccups, you must expel it and inquire about its initial stage with an instrument that is called "intromes", according to its form which will be explained in the following chapter.
And this is the method of inquiry for abscesses and all types of hiccups: you should take this instrument (intromes) and insert it gently into the moistest location you find on the abscess, rotating the instrument slowly until you are certain that it has penetrated the membrane.

Because if any residual cause remains, whether small or large, the hiccup will return with greater intensity.
And if you notice that a small part of it remains, then complete the wound with some corrosive powders and strengthen the wound, placing a cauterizing agent on the abscess, and cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
And if the hiccup is large, then you should suture both lips of it and cure it with that which causes it to suppurate (encarnar).

Chapter 2: On the section of abscesses, which occur in the cheek and those that occur in the belly.
It often happens that abscesses develop in the bellies of people and in other parts of their bodies, which are called "fungal" due to their similarity to fungi, and their structure is subtle and their heads are thick; and already the lips of these have turned inward, and some are small, while others are greatly enlarged.

Chapter 2.
Chapter 2: On the treatment of a protrusion of the navel.
A protrusion of the navel can be caused by many factors, such as tears in the ciphac (a membrane or fascia that covers the abdomen), which can lead to the herniation of tissue or organs through the resulting opening; or it may be due to bleeding from a vein or artery near the navel, which can cause swelling and inflammation; or it may be caused by an obstruction in the intestines or other digestive organs that leads to gas buildup and pressure on the navel.
But if the protrusion is due to tears in the ciphac and herniation of tissue or organs, then the color of the abscess will be similar to that of the surrounding skin; it will typically be painless, but may appear in various shapes and sizes depending on the location and extent of the hernia. But if the protrusion is due to herniation of the bowel or intestines, then the location and appearance of the hernia will depend on the position of the affected organ and the degree of obstruction. When you press on it with your fingers, it may temporarily disappear, only to return when you release the pressure. This type of protrusion is often associated with severe pain and discomfort, as well as difficulty passing stool or gas due to the obstruction.
But if it is due to moisture or fluid buildup, then the protrusion will be painless and not hidden when you press on it with your hand. It will not feel tight or swollen.
And if it is due to bleeding, then the protrusion will be accompanied by these signs: the abscess will have a dark color that is declining or fading.
But if it is due to thickened or hardened tissue, then the protrusion will be a severe abscess that is large and hard, and will have a distinct size or shape.
But if it is due to gas or wind, then touching it will be painless.
And the operation for this is that you should consider whether the protrusion of the navel is due to bleeding from an artery or a vein, or from gas. If it is, then you must not attempt to treat it, as there is danger and fear involved in such cases, just as we have taught you in the chapter where we discussed abscesses caused by arteries and veins.
And if the swelling of the navel is due to the intestines or membranes, then you must instruct the patient to hold their belly, and stand extended; and approach carefully examine the entire area around the navel, and then command them to lie down between your hands upon their back, and then place a spatula along the circumference of the navel at the marked location; and then drain the abscess in the area above with a large incision; and then bind it in the circumference with strong ligature or ceda and in the appropriate manner.
And then you should insert your finger into the middle of the abscess and push it down onto the ligament, searching for the intestine; and if you have found or protected it through the ligament, then you should extract gently and guide the intestines back to their place in the interior of the belly.
And if you have found membranes, then take hold of them with a forceps and make an incision into the superfluous part.
But if it is contrary to your incision or vein, then you should circle that part and return to your operation; and take two needles and place strong ligatures on both of them and insert two needles into the circuit which you have made around the abscess in a cross shape, causing them to penetrate; and then hold the abscess in four parts onto the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and leave the area so that the flesh can extend itself and fall by itself; or make an incision when it is thinned out and possible, and then heal that with what is necessary of ointments until it heals.
And if the swelling of the navel is due to thickened flesh or moisture, then it is appropriate that you make an incision in the abscess as we have said and drain the blood or moisture which you find inside, and then heal that with what is necessary and strengthen the area.
Chapter 53
Of the treatment of cancer.
We have already said in the division of the types of cancer and what method is used for its healing with medicines, that it is advisable to treat it with iron to prevent ulcers; and we have said that cancer requires caution and care in its treatment.
And the ancients have said that some cancers are in places where it is possible to extract them entirely, such as cancer of the breast or thigh and similar ones located on limbs which can be removed entirely, especially when they are small and beginning.

Chapter 60: On the removal of a stone.
We have already discussed in the previous sections the types of stones and their treatment with medicines, as well as the difference between stones generated in the kidneys and those generated in the bladder, and the symptoms that accompany them.
And we have mentioned that a stone can be operated on with the hand and sectioning.
And a bladder stone, properly speaking, is one that is located in the bladder.
I will now describe this in clear and concise terms.
I say that bladder stones are most commonly found in children, and the symptoms of this condition include urine that is thin and watery like water when it is expelled from the bladder, and sand or grit may be present in the urine. The patient will also experience pain and a frequent urge to urinate, and they may have difficulty starting or stopping their flow of urine. In addition, they may notice blood in their urine or experience rectal pain when passing urine.
The treatment of bladder stones in children is usually successful before they reach the age of 14, but it can be difficult to treat in older individuals. But in young people, the treatment is easier because it occurs within them.
And the treatment of bladder stones is easier when they are larger, but if they are small, the opposite is true.
Therefore, in order to treat a bladder stone, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, which will extract any feces or debris that may be obstructing the path of the stone. This is important because fecal matter can sometimes prevent the stone from being expelled naturally or make surgical removal more difficult. By cleansing the bowel prior to surgery, healthcare providers can help ensure a clearer and less obstructed path for the stone, making it easier to locate and remove during the procedure. This can help reduce the risk of complications and improve the overall outcomes for the patient.
And then the patient should be positioned with their legs drawn up and strapped down in order to encourage the stone to descend towards the opening of the bladder, or to move out of its current location. This can help facilitate the removal of the stone during surgery by allowing it to be more easily accessed and extracted from the urinary tract. By positioning the patient in this way, healthcare providers can help ensure a smoother and more successful surgical intervention.
And then apply a cupping glass to the lower part of the patient's abdomen in order to draw the bladder downward and make it more accessible during surgery. This can be done by placing the cup over the affected area and creating a vacuum seal, which will help draw the bladder closer to the surface of the skin. By doing this, healthcare providers can create a clearer path for the surgical instruments and improve the overall outcomes of the procedure.
And then carefully extract the stone and remove it entirely from the body. This is an important step in the surgical process, as any remaining fragments or pieces of the stone can potentially cause further complications or lead to recurrent symptoms in the future. By carefully extracting the entire stone during surgery, healthcare providers can help ensure a successful outcome for the patient and minimize the risk of future issues related to bladder stones.

Chapter LXII (62).
On incision for hernia strangulation.
An inguinal hernia is nothing but an accumulation of fluid in the white membrane located near the groin and containing the liquid, which is called scrotum.

And the signs by which it is known where this accumulation of fluid is located are: if it is in the white membrane that we mentioned, then the abscess will be round and slightly elongated, similar to the shape of an egg, and the genitals will appear, as the fluid will surround them from all sides.
And if the fluid is in the proper fatty tissue, then the abscess will be round with an opening similar to that of an egg, and for this reason, people think it is another testicle.
And if the fluid is between the cord of the genitalia and the white membrane, then there will be a sensation of heaviness in that area.
And if you want to determine the color of the fluid, then press on the abscess with a curved probe whose shape is known; and according to what comes out in the trace of the probe, make your judgment based on that.
And so when we come to the treatment of it with surgery, then it is advisable to order the patient to undergo venesection if it is possible for you, and also puncture the abscess.

But if the testicle protrudes from its cord during your operation, then after you have completed the incision of the white membrane, return it inside and then close the two sides of the inguinal cord with sutures, and take care of it as you would other wounds until it is healed.
And if you find the testicle has become corrupt due to some other disease, then it is necessary to cut the vessels that are over the suspensory ligament and remove the testicle, and take care of it as we have said before.
But if the fluid is accumulated in two separate parts, then you should know that there are two hernias; therefore, make an incision in one part as you did in the other, and if it seems to you that it is one operation, then you perform it.
And then you should clean the blood and introduce wool soaked in oil or rose oil into the incisions, and place another piece of wool outside that has been soaked in wine and oil, spreading it over the genitals and the umbilical area; and put cloths folded and dampened with water on top, and bind them with a bandage that is made as follows:
And then two cloths should be prepared and stuffed with red wool in the following manner; the ends of which are pressed together with string or wet wool, and attached with compression inside the breeches, one end taking hold of the buttocks from behind, and the other at the division of the umbilical area, and both ends placed over two thighs below and two others over two kidneys, and all the compression should be adjusted inside the breeches.
And sometimes this hernia is treated artificially with cautery instead of incision with a knife; and it is done by taking a thin cauterizing scalpel and making an incision with it in the cord of the genitals, and then igniting it as we have said before until the white membrane containing the fluid is exposed. And you should take cautery in the following form: And it is shaped like the Greek letter L.
And then puncture the white membrane with it (cautery), and ignite it until all the fluid is removed.
And approach the hip with forceps, and scrape with forceps, and scrape with a sharp cautery heated; and make an incision in the second one that is possible for you to cut out completely; and be careful that the fire does not touch the fluid.
And know that this operation is safer and further away from bleeding than an incision, and better than surgery with cutting.
But if you have an abscess or bleeding during the incision or cauterization, then you must treat the condition that arises accordingly, with treatment that is suitable based on what has been said.
But if the patient is weak and does not expect a second operation due to its horror, then administer puncturing as I have recommended; and this is when you are certain, based on what has been said about the signs, that the hernia is watery.
Then it is necessary that you lay the patient on an elevated cushion, approach and puncture the abscess in its lowest part with a broad-bladed spatula, and place the puncture according to the length of the body.
And let the incision be wide enough to allow all the water to flow out.
And then place a finger over the opening and press it gently, allowing the remaining water to flow out. And then heal the wound until the injury is cured.
But if there is an obstruction to the flow of water at that time, then you should puncture it: and this should not be done unless the whitish granulation tissue in the opening of the wound creates an obstruction and prevents the outflow of water, in which case it is necessary to insert a probe or instrument used for extracting water from hydropics into the wound, the shape of which has been described; or apply pressure to the edges of the wound with a small piece of wood.
And know that the water returns and accumulates again after two or three months; and when it has accumulated, then it should be punctured in the same manner, for the patient will thus pass his days.
Chapter 63.
Of incision on a fatty hernia and its healing.
Know that in the incision of this hernia there is fear of danger, even in the best circumstances; therefore, I recommend avoiding it and choosing the safest option instead.
And I remember the operation on that one and the types of abscesses.
Therefore, I say that an abscess is formed in the parts of the body where the veins are congested and this happens for many reasons: either due to sudden and severe congestion, which spreads to the veins, or due to trauma.
And the color of an abscess is similar to that of the body part where it forms, and pain is not present in it, and it is a serious abscess.
And a hard abscess is one that is filled with pus, whose color is dark and there is no sensation in it.
And sometimes abscesses are formed by congestion of the arteries, and this is noticeable because there is a memory of it, or due to inflammation of veins.
But abscesses caused by inflammation of the arteries can be recognized by the spreading of the abscess when you press it with your fingers, and it is not advisable to touch it.
But an abscess caused by inflammation of a vein does not spread when you press it with your fingers due to the compression of the vein.
And it is possible to make an incision on this type of abscess and on other parts of the body: that is, you should cut into the skin of the groin, pull the skin upwards, extract the whitish pus from the cavity, release the suspensory ligament of the veins, tie them off, and incise the suspensory ligament more than you have released it from all parts of the cavity of the veins.
Therefore, if the fluid has already solidified with the surrounding flesh, then it is necessary to extract the fluid and make an incision into that area.
And if there is an adhesion between the flesh for some reason, or between what is between the veins, then it is necessary to release all of that adhesion and make a round incision into it.
But if there is a growth of flesh in the place of the adhesion which is behind it, then it is necessary to cut into all of that, and extract the fluid as I have said.
Therefore, when the operation is complete, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, and take care of it with the other treatment until it heals.

Chapter 64
A hernia (vit) is an abscess enclosed by a membrane similar to a blister, accompanied by swelling of the testicles, making movement and walking difficult for the patient.
And in the treatment of this condition, caution is advised due to the risk associated with its onset.
However, we must also discuss surgery as a second option after the first has been attempted.
And I say that the patient should be laid on an elevated table, and the surgeon should carefully lift up the scrotum and tie off the spermatic cord near the inguinal canal using a ligature that has been tested on a piece of string. The other assistants should also hold the patient's limbs firmly in place, stretching them as needed.
And then make an incision with a narrow, sharp scalpel along the length of the vessels until they are exposed.
And then remove the outer layer of tissue from all parts of the area, just as we described in the extraction of abscesses in the temples.
And then place a needle with double thread into the area, and tie it at the first point where the hernia occurs, and tie the other end at the back of the area. And then make a straight incision along the length of the body in the middle area, and remove any material that has accumulated due to putrefied and corrupted fluids.
And then treat the wound as you would any other wound where infection is likely to occur, in order to prevent any damage to the vessels that supply blood to one or both of the testicles, as this could lead to serious complications.
However, if the hernia has affected all of the blood vessels, then it is necessary to remove the testicles entirely or to allow them to atrophy due to lack of nutrients from the severed blood vessels. This will prevent any further damage and ensure that they do not interfere with the healing process.
Chapter 65.
Chapter 65: On the treatment of intestinal hernia.
The occurrence of this hernia is due to a rupture in the fascia, which extends over the abdomen from the inguinal region of the pelvis. When the intestines protrude through this weakened area, they can become trapped and cause obstruction or strangulation.
This rupture can be caused by either the ciphac or a weakness in it, and it can occur for various reasons such as impact, strain, loud noises, heavy lifting, or similar causes.
The sign of this type of hernia, when it is caused by the extension of the fascia, is that it develops gradually over a long period of time and does not occur suddenly. It may also be accompanied by a swelling or abscess near the inguinal region, which occurs because the fascia is compressing the intestines.
The sign of this type of hernia, when it is caused by a rupture in the fascia, is that it initially causes sudden and severe pain, accompanied by a swelling or abscess that appears differently than a typical inguinal hernia. This occurs because the intestine is protruding through the damaged fascial tissue and becoming inflamed.
In some cases, the intestine may protrude through a hole in the abdominal wall along with a portion of the peritoneum (the lining of the abdominal cavity), which is known as a Richter's hernia or zirbal hernia.
In some cases, the hernia may be caused by gas in the intestine, and in other cases it may occur when a portion of the intestine becomes trapped in a tear or fissure. This can lead to serious complications such as intestinal obstruction or strangulation, which can be life-threatening if not treated promptly.
And in the treatment of this condition with iron (i.e., surgery), there is a risk of complications, which is why it is important to avoid injury or damage to surrounding tissues during the procedure.
The method of surgery for this condition involves instructing the patient to manually reduce the intestine back into their abdominal cavity using their own hand, while the surgeon applies gentle pressure to assist in the process. The patient is then positioned on their side with a pillow or other support beneath their pelvis to maintain proper alignment and prevent further herniation.
The surgeon should then carefully dissect the tissue surrounding the inguinal canal, isolating and cutting the spermatic cord with sharp scissors. They should then create two small incisions on either side of the incision, inserting curved needles or forceps to gently separate the edges of the incision and facilitate closure.
If the incision is larger than necessary, or if there is a risk of tissue herniation through the surgical site, the surgeon may choose to use a mesh reinforcement to strengthen the abdominal wall and prevent future hernias from developing.
The surgeon should then carefully remove any excess fascial tissue or adhesions from the inguinal canal, exposing the underlying white, fibrous tissue of the transversalis fascia. This will allow for precise identification and repair of any defects in the abdominal wall that may be contributing to the hernia.
After this, the surgeon should carefully dissect the tissue surrounding the spermatic cord and testicle, isolating and dividing any adhesions or attachments between the transversalis fascia and the surrounding structures. This will allow for careful mobilization of the testicle and repair of the hernia defect without tension or undue strain on the surrounding tissues.
The surgeon should then place their hand over the testicle, gently guiding it back into its normal position outside of the abdominal wall. They should use their other hand to carefully stretch and retract the transversalis fascia laterally, creating more space for the hernia repair. Once sufficient space has been created, they can elevate the testicle and hernia sac back up to the level of the incision, using gentle traction to align everything properly. The assistant should then apply downward pressure on the testicle, holding it in place while the surgeon carefully dissects and divides any remaining adhesions or attachments between the transversalis fascia and the surrounding structures, using a combination of blunt and sharp dissection as needed.
And ask with your words if there is any cause for the intestine being wrapped in the hard white diaphragm. But if you find any cause in him, then you should push it down to his belly.
And then make an incision below the kidneys, in the section where blood and pus flow, as we have said before.
And then apply wool soaked in oil to the wound and place it on the incision; and apply the ligature that we mentioned (and sometimes the white diaphragm is cauterized, which we said before should be feared for the risk of bleeding during the incision, because this happens frequently); and leave the ligature in place until it falls off by itself.
But if the scab is slow to form, then apply hot water and place it on top, as we have said.
And then care for the wound with the same treatment used for other wounds until it is healed.
Chapter 66.
On hernia ventosa (or "windy hernia").
In this type of hernia, I have not seen anyone who has been bold enough to attempt a cure using iron.
And the first [doctors] said that it should be treated in the same way as we have described for hernia that is alive; that is, you should tie off the veins near the incision with ease, and dry up the surrounding area around the abscess using a substance that causes it to shrink, until the veins fall away.
And care for the wound in the way that we have described until it is healed.
Chapter 67.
On the disruption (or "dislocation" or "disruption of continuity") that occurs in the sinews (or "tendons" or "ligaments").
Sometimes there is a rupture in the tendons or ligaments, as we have said, and they protrude from the affected area.
And one should not allow any cause of the intestines to reach the groin; and if it does, it is only a little; and it always returns.
But if this condition persists for a long time, then a fissure forms in the diaphragm, allowing the intestines to protrude into the thoracic cavity; and this happens because of the stretching of the diaphragm that occurs in the tendons or ligaments, as we have said. The cause of this is that the diaphragm is stretched out, making it weak and thin, and the area becomes abscessed and protrudes.
And the treatment for this condition is with a hot iron, as we have described earlier.
And sometimes this condition is treated with iron in the following way: the patient lies on their back with their legs extended and open, and the area of the rupture or protrusion of the abscess is dried using a hot iron along its length, equivalent to three finger-widths.
And then strengthen the white diaphragm that is below the kidney so that it is exposed.
And then take a rod and place it on the protruding area of the diaphragm, and press it against the pressure point of the abdomen.
And then sew together the two protruding areas on either end of the rod that is placed on the diaphragm, using a suture to join them.
And then remove the end of the rod, but do not make a complete incision in the diaphragm, and do not release any fluid or cause any other damage, as you know in the treatment of intestinal hernia.
And then care for this condition with the same treatment used for wounds, and when you make incisions in the abscess, clean it and restore the wound until it is consolidated; because the diaphragm is contracted and the protrusion of the rupture is not adjusted.
And cauterization is better in this location, because it is closer to health.
Chapter 68.
On the softening of the kidney of the testicles.
Much observation has shown that the spermatic cord in some men is softened because the flesh between them is softened, and this requires careful monitoring.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one treating the patient to have them lie on their back and to secure the entire spermatic cord that has become softened onto the natural spermatic cord; and then carefully stitch together the two labia (of the scrotum).
And if desired, in the beginning, excessively softened parts of the spermatic cord can be excised with three or four sutures and firm stitches.
Then insert between the sutures; and then take care of healing any other wounds inside until it is healed and pus disappears.
Chapter 69.
On castration.
Know that castration is forbidden in our religion, but it is appropriate for me to mention it in this book; and there are two reasons why I should bring it up: the first is so that a doctor, when questioned about it, would have knowledge of its treatment; and the second reason is that we often need castration of other animals for our livestock, such as horses, oxen, pigs, and similar animals.
And so I say that castration is performed in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting in half.
But in that which is performed by crushing, the method of operation is to submerge the animal in hot water until its genitals become soft and limp and hang down. Then hold those in your hand until they are drained and do not show through the covering.
But in castration performed by cutting and splitting, it is necessary to hold the animal and press down on the spermatic cord of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie up the suspensory ligament and make a cut into each one of them between two protrusions.
Then remove any excess skin that you have excised. And do not leave anything on the outside of it, but make a subtle incision that is above the veins.
And this method of castration performed by crushing is better because it leaves some parts of the testicles intact, which makes the animal still have a desire to mate.
Then take care of the wound until it heals.
Chapter 70.
On the treatment of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in men occurs in two ways: the first is when there is a space between the scrotum and the testicles, where there appears to be a woman's vulva between the two testicles.
And sometimes, the person's urine comes out from the space between the testicles.
But in women, there is a different type: and that is when the vulva above the pubic bone appears to be like two male testicles, slightly protruding outside as if they were a man's penis and scrotum.
And the treatment is of three types: two for males and one for females. And it is necessary to cut the swollen flesh and return it inside so that it heals, and then take care of any other wounds.
And in the second type of males, where urine comes out from the space between the testicles, there is no cure or treatment for them.
Chapter 71.
On leanness and protruding flesh due to causes in women.
Leanness is easily corrected due to natural causes when it becomes prominent and requires careful attention; sometimes, it can become so extreme in some women that it spreads as much as in men and even prevents sexual intercourse.
Then it is necessary to hold the excess leanness with your hand or a tool and remove it by cutting.
And do not cut too deeply, especially near the navel, to avoid causing bleeding.
Then heal that wound as you would any other wound until it is healed.
But flesh that is born is flesh that grows inside the womb until it fills it up, and it easily protrudes outside in the shape of a tail (and for this reason, I will call this condition "caudal disease" for now); therefore, it is necessary to cut it like we would leanness, and heal the wound until it is healed.
Chapter 72.
On the treatment of hernia.
Hernia refers to when a woman's vulva is not perforated or has a small perforation. And it can be either natural or accidental.
An accidental hernia is caused by an underlying illness and can occur due to loose flesh or thin or thick skin.
An accidental hernia can occur in the navel of the mother, near the ribs, or above or below it, and it prevents sexual intercourse, pregnancy, and menstruation.
The diagnosis of a hernia is made by examining the mother's belly button and determining if it is prominent; but if it is not visible, then use your fingers or an instrument to examine it.
But if the hernia is caused by thin skin and appears near the two labia, then you should press down on it and break it open.
And place your fingers on the two labia and then press both of your index fingers firmly against them.
And the woman should be lying on her back with her thighs extended and use force to open up the two labia until that thin skin is broken and the opening is visible.
Then take some wool and soak it in oil and place it over the wound to prevent the cut from becoming solidified; and have someone stay with her for several days to ensure that the wound does not become infected.
But if the skin is thick and hard, then it is necessary to cut into it with a scalpel or myrtle leaf.
But if the hernia is caused by loose flesh, then use forceps to lift up the flesh and cut into it.
And use the following medicines to stop bleeding without causing pain, such as henbane, dragon's blood, and alum boiled in egg white.
And then administer a wide leaden cannula so that the wound does not heal lightly.
And leave it there for several days and apply heat to it.
And then it should be cured with another method of solidification until it is healed.
And sometimes it happens that during the birth of other animals, (it) is necessary to proceed in this manner. But if this is due to a hard abscess, in the case of a hard abscess in the mother, it should not be treated with iron in any way.
Chapter 73.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, piles, and red botches that occur in the female genital area.
Hemorrhoids are the swelling of the orifices of many veins, from which a large amount of blood flows continuously; and when hemorrhoids become old and form lumps.

But those that are in the opening of the mother's womb, over which a sensation can be felt, those are the ones that are cured.

And then wrap her legs with bandages for an hour and then place her in cold water.

And if blood is separated, it's good; and if not, make it stick with two suction cups, and on the nipples, make scars.

Chapter 74.
On the rupture or accidental injury in the mother.
Many types of abscesses that occur in the mother, such as hard and stony abscesses, ulcers, abscesses with pus, herpes, fistulous hemorrhoids, fissures, tumors, and other abscesses. And I have already said these illnesses and the types of them and their signs, and their cures, in the division.
