Capital LXXV [Note: This is simply indicating the beginning of the seventy-fifth chapter or section of the medical treatise.]
To teach midwives how fetal bodies are treated when they are born according to an unnatural shape.
It is necessary for the midwife to know in the beginning the shape of a normal childbirth by its signs, and that when you see the woman pushing from below and desires to smell fresh air, and is relieved because the delivery is coming, and she hastens the birth of the infant, then you will know that this birth is according to natural shape, and it occurs with the birth over its head, and the afterbirth attached or hanging from the umbilical cord. [**Note: This translation is based on my understanding of medieval medical texts and some knowledge in obstetrics, but I am not a doctor. Please consult modern medical texts for accurate information.**]
Therefore, when you see those signs, then it is necessary to press on the woman's abdomen gently so that the fetus descends slowly. For when it emerges over its head, give the afterbirth to the infant and clean it of superfluidities with good cleaning.
But if this is another type of birth that is unnatural and not desirable, for when the infant emerges on its feet and the body comes out in front of its head and one leg or foot is first. Or it emerges with the head and one arm or the belly, and it turns over quickly onto its neck, similar to the shape of undesirable forms.
Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be knowledgeable and skilled in all of these cases and that she protect herself from errors and deceptions.
And I have shown you the entire figure of those [cases], and what type of ingenuity is involved in each one, so that it may be understood and become clear to you.
When the baby emerges over its head through natural effort and is very heavy on the woman and makes delivery difficult, and sometimes its strength has already been weakened, then do this: make her lie down or have her hold it, and apply a poultice of fenugreek and warm oils to her stomach.
And then the midwife inserts her small spatula and splits open the afterbirth or cuts it with her fingernail until what is inside of it, which is wet, runs out. And press on the woman's abdomen until the baby descends.

And if the two hands of the baby are forgotten at the beginning, then it is necessary to reduce those with ease gradually, little by little. But if the limbs are not returned and the baby dies, then enter in and extract the contents of the baby or attach the corpse to the hand with a cloth and extract it equally, because it will soon be forgotten.
When the fetus is lying on its feet, you should massage its legs and gently turn it over, bind its feet together, and then gradually stretch them out by taking hold of one foot at a time.
But if it has already come out between the thighs, then you should instruct the woman to push, and make her sneeze with caution, as this could cause it to be expelled if God wills it.[Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ]

And also perform a gentle cedar bath for her, until she feels relief in her hypochondria (the area just below the ribcage).

Ensuring the safety of a transverse presentation of the fetus, with one arm up. The fetus should be repositioned to reduce the raised arm, but if that is not possible, then elevate the woman's hips and have her change position. [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ]

Instruct her to sneeze with caution.[Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] The delivery of a prepared fetus on its side.
When the membranes are about to come out of the mother's vagina in this manner, observe and then gently insert your fingernail into the cervix until it is dilated and emptied of fluid.
If the fetus is stuck with its face and neck facing up, then gently insert your finger covered in emblic (a type of herb) to ensure it is not obstructed or delayed.
And then gently push the fetus towards the birth canal until it is in the correct position, and encourage the woman to push several times. If God wills it, the baby will be born with gentle effort.[Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ]
The delivery of twins or multiple fetuses. Be aware that often twins are born in multiple deliveries, and sometimes even three or four, but this is rare and usually happens due to natural causes, resulting in stillbirths.
Count the number of fetuses, whether multiple or not, as one cervix. Separate each one by using a doubled finger to distinguish them from the ligaments in their umbilical cord. Some may be born easily with gentle effort, while others require more difficult labor, as previously recommended. [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ]
If the delivery of twins or multiple fetuses is difficult and requires non-natural positions, then care for them as previously described.
If the midwife is skilled and performs her duties with ease, subtlety, and patience, she should use all means necessary to ensure a safe delivery.[Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ]
A reminder that a fetus can be formed in the womb from multiple embryos and may be aborted.
Some women have formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and even ten fetuses, and now I can confirm that one woman aborts or gives birth to five fetuses, while another delivers ten, a difference caused by the measurement of the glorious wise ones.
It is important for midwives to be knowledgeable about such cases, as they may encounter them and must act accordingly.[Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ]
Chapter seventy-six.
On the extraction of a dead fetus.
When dealing with a stillborn fetus using the methods described in the division of medicine and it does not come out naturally, you may need to use manual extraction techniques. However, before doing so, consider whether the woman is healthy and free from any conditions that could put her life at risk during the procedure. [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗʰ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] [Ⅰᶤˡʸ ᵗþ ᶜᵒ ᵈᶦᶜᵉ ᶜᵘᵖ-ˢ ˡᶦᶜʸ] ...]
Now it is necessary that the woman be positioned lying on her side on the bed, with her head lowered and her buttocks raised.
The assistant should hold her from both sides or be lying in the bed with her, so that her body does not extend during the delivery of the baby.
And then you should moisten the mother's mouth with warm oil and marshmallow and fenugreek and linseed.
And then anoint the midwife's hand with those oils and mucilages, and then insert her hand easily into the mother, and then search with your hand for the location where you can hook the fetus with your fingers.
And do this at the right spot: then you consider if the fetus is ready to come out by its head, and then hook it by the heels or the neck or the mouth or the palate or under the chin or on the shoulder blades or below the ribs.
But if it is coming out by its feet, then hook it in the ankle or in the middle of the ribs.
And it is necessary to bend the fingers of your right hand in a curve and place this curvature in the spot that is between the said fingers of your left hand, and then insert your hand easily and hook one of those spots I mentioned, until you reach the membrane.
And then place and insert another finger or the third one if necessary, in order to provide traction and not only extension according to its natural shape.
But it should be done on all sides, in order for the extraction to be eased, just like it is done with a tooth during its extraction.
And it is necessary in this that the extension be softened; and if some part of it is retained, then the midwife should anoint her fingers with oil and insert them skillfully and rotate what is retained.
Therefore, if a part of the fetus is prolapsed, then the fingers should be inserted into another spot that is more accessible; and do this until the entire fetus is extracted.
But if one hand is in front of the other and it is not possible to reduce it due to its swelling, then a cloth should be wrapped around it; and then extract it until all of it is outside, and insert it into the wrist joint or the armpit.
And you should do the same with the other hand and both feet.
But if the fetus's head is large, or if it is swollen during delivery, or if there is water accumulated in its head, then you should insert your fingers between the said vertebrae and break open the head and extract the water, or you should make an incision with a tool called "alundat", whose form will be provided with the other tools in the chapter that comes next.
And similarly do if the fetus has a large head naturally: and then insert it with forceps, or take it out with an "alundat" as we said before; and then extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is out but stuck at the shoulders, then it should be broken open so that the fluid in the feet can be drained.
But if it is not complicated or obstructed during delivery, then you should immediately insert your fingers into the head as much as possible.
And if the left side of the abdomen is abscessed or hydropic, then you should pierce it in order to drain the fluid that is inside.
But if the fetus is on its feet, then the traction of it is light and the direction to the mother's womb is easy.
But if it is stuck between the belly and the feet, then you should extract it with a cloth that you have wrapped around your hand, and then break open the belly and the feet in order to drain what is inside.
But if the other limbs are obstructed and the head turns back, then the midwife should insert her left hand; but if the mother's womb is opened, then she should insert her hand into the membrane and search for the head with it, and pull it towards the mother's womb using her fingers. Then she should insert one or two fingers into it and pull it with those.
But if the mother's womb is obstructed by an abscess caused by a stone that forms in the uterus, then it should not be pressed on; instead, it is necessary to administer a flow of warm and fatty liquids. And administer poultices; and follow the treatment with warm and moist baths.
And if the fetus is on its side, then if possible it should be turned over; and administer what we said in the case of a live fetus.
And if that is not possible, then insert your fingers into the vagina and extract it.
And it is necessary that you do not leave any cause behind in the secondine (afterbirth).
And once you have completed your entire operation, then administer what we said about the treatment for abscesses that occur in the mother's uterus.
And if there is a flow of blood, then immerse her in styptic waters and administer the other treatment.
And I have seen a woman in whose womb there was a dead fetus, and then another pregnancy occurred over it, and the second fetus was also dead. It happened to a man that for a long time there was an abscess in his navel; and it became so swollen that it burst open, and he began to vomit bile.
And I was called upon to treat him, and I treated him for a long time, but the wound did not heal.
Then I applied strong-attraction plasters to him made of certain causes, and a bone came out of him, and after passing several days another bone came out; and I was greatly amazed that there could be bones in his belly.
And then I thought that they were bones from the dead fetus.
Then I explored the wound and extracted many bones from it, the woman being in her menstrual periods; and she lived for a long time afterwards, with only a small amount of bile coming up (vomiting).
And I did not think it strange, because in that there is knowledge and help for the physician who uses his hands to administer treatment.
The forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
The form of forceps with which the mother is opened.
This is the form of "strenhedor" in which the loins are held, to which holding there are two forceps at the ends of two rods. However, this forceps must be more subtle than the strictor, and it should be made of ivory or boxwood.
And the width of each rod is two fingers and the edge of each is one finger, and the length of each is a palm and a half; and in the middle of the two rods there are two fittings of that same rod which are already fastened, whose length is the majority of a palm and a little more, and the width of each is two fingers or slightly more.
And these two ingredients should be inserted in the mouth of the mother to keep it open when you turn the two prescribed screws.
Another similar form, but even more subtle and lighter:
Make it out of a wooden or boxwood handle, in the shape of forceps. However, at the end of its two extensions, there should be as seen, and the length of these extensions should be about a palm's length, and the width of each one should be two fingers.
And when you want to use these to open the mouth of the patient, make her lean back on a bed with her legs hanging down and an opening between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument as you would with forceps, according to how much of the opening of the patient's mouth you want to enter, until you achieve what you want.
The form of torture that the ancients called "vertigo":
A device for propelling or moving an object, which is used to move the abscess:
A device for containing or restraining, used to contain a large head:
And it is made like forceps with teeth at the end, as seen, and sometimes it is made long like forceps of this type, as seen, with teeth like those of a saw, which are inserted and used to contain or restrain. A device for containing or supporting, in a small form:
The form of a hook with a spine:
The form of a hook with two spines:
The form of a spatula with two ends, used to cut or remove the head:
The form of two flat spatulas:
All of these instruments should be practiced with and once their species are multiplied and prepared by the craftsmen, they must be made as light as possible in their operation and as easy to use for people according to their size.
And you should not neglect using any of these instruments when it is necessary, because their necessity cannot be avoided.
On the extraction of the second teeth.
When the second tooth is impacted, you should command the patient to bite on their finger, and then make them sneeze with caution. Place your hand over their mouth and nose, and if it comes out as a result, that's good.
And if not, you should take a piece of cloth and make a hole in it, and place herbs that are soaked in the mouth of the mother, such as chamomile and rue and anise and camphor and Arabic gum and cinnamon bark and frankincense. All of these herbs or some of them should be soaked in water in the cloth, and then placed over the fire.
Then place a reed cannula in the mouth of the mother, and keep it inside so that the vapor reaches the cavity of the mother.
Then make her sneeze as we mentioned before, and the second tooth will be extracted quickly.
But if this treatment is not successful and the tooth remains impacted, you should then command the midwife to submerge her left hand in olive oil or marshmallow mucilage, and then insert it into the cavity and near the second tooth, until she finds it. When she has found it, take hold of it gently, pulling it out little by little as directed, so that the mother does not feel pain from the violent attraction. It is necessary that she be able to move her right and left sides with ease.
And if the mother's mouth is constricted, we have already recommended treatment with sneezing and herbal medicine applied with a cloth.
But if it is not extracted with all the causes we have recommended, you must be careful not to continue to extract from her in an iterative process of abstraction. Instead, what has come out of her should be brought to the thigh of the woman and covered with a mixture of egg white, honey, turpentine, and frankincense; because this will cause it to rot within a few days and dissolve and become extracted.
But when it is rotten, it causes great harm to the head and stomach of the patient, and this harms her. Therefore, it is necessary to administer sub-fumigations that are suitable for this.
But many of the Ancients used sub-fumigation with mustard seeds and dried figs.
The form of an instrument used for sub-fumigation of the woman to treat menstrual retention and impacted teeth:
It is made of iron or copper.
And the thin end should be placed in the cavity and the wide end over the fire, and the sub-fumigation should be directed towards the coals of the fire.
And keep that inside until the sub-fumigation is consumed, then repeat another one.
On the treatment of a non-perforated infant's buttocks.
The words of infants bite and their buttocks are not perforated, which appear thin and sunken. Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that sunken area with her finger; and if not, then pierce it with a sharp spatula, and make sure not to touch the vein.
And then place some wool soaked in wine and oil on it, and treat the area with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
But if you are concerned that it may become sunken again, then place a reed in the hole for several days and remove it when the child no longer needs it.

Of the suture of hemorrhoids in which blood runs in the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the anus like charcoal, or those that resemble lumps of raisins. And some are small and large, and blood constantly runs from them, they are one and many, they are outside the anus, and at their edges.

The treatment for internal hemorrhoids is to instruct the patient to sit on a hard surface and express themselves until the anus relaxes and the hemorrhoids become visible to you. A wart (veruca) is a small, rough, round, fistulated elevation on the surface of the body, and they are very common in children.
The treatment for warts is to either incise and cut it out, or apply a poultice of crushed garlic or animal fat on it until it falls off. And if desired, cauterize (the area) with fire or a caustic medicine, as mentioned earlier.
A mole (formica) is a small, raised or fistulated, hard growth on the surface of the body that resembles a ant bite when touched, and it can be found anywhere on the body.
The treatment for moles is to take a quill from a rooster or vulture feather, and make sure it is sturdy. Place the quill directly over the mole so that its circumference covers the entire growth. Then, rotate your hand around the quill while pressing down firmly, until you have incised the area around the mole. Next, press the quill into the flesh to remove the mole from its root.

Here are some examples of medical instruments used in surgery:
Sometimes surgery is performed using silver or lead or iron instruments, and sometimes other types of instruments are used depending on the procedure. The size of the instrument should be appropriate for the patient, especially when treating young children. The form of large-scale surgery is as follows:
The top of the cannula should be wide enough to accommodate the attached pouch, and it should have a clear distinguishing mark where the pouch is attached.
And the lower end of the probe, which enters into the wound, should be blunt and rounded, with a pointed tip that tapers gradually to a fine point. On one side of the probe, there should be two notches or indentations, and on the opposite side, there should be a single notch. The width of each notch should correspond to the thickness of the surrounding tissue, but they should be only slightly wider than the tip of the probe.
And the pouch that holds the medicines should be made from a bladder of an animal or sheepskin, and its size should be about the width of a handspan.
And it should be pierced with many holes, as it is rolled up; and the spaces between the holes should be about the width of a finger.
Then insert strong, raw garlic (made from ten cloves) or something similar into those holes and attach the pouch to it. When the pouch is placed on the wound, make sure it fits snugly around the top of the surgical instrument with strong compression, and cauterize each hole using that instrument. However, the method for cauterizing with that instrument is to fill the pouch with heated medicine according to the patient's tolerance, making sure it is not too hot or too cold.
Then have the patient lie down on their back with their legs elevated and place a heavy object, such as a stone or a large book, under their hips to keep them in that position. Have an assistant hold the pouch and squeeze it firmly with both hands to expel all the contents from the cannula into the intestines. After that, remove the cautery instrument and have the patient get up slowly while keeping their legs elevated.
And if the medicine forces you to urinate, then do so as much as possible. If you can sleep with it for a whole night, it will be more beneficial.

Treatment of wounds/sores.
I have already mentioned in the classification of wound treatment what is necessary for this book, and now I will say how to treat wounds with my methods and medications according to their severity.
I say that wounds are classified according to what causes them and where they are located on the body.
And the causes by which wounds are often made include: striking with a stone, cutting with a sword or knife, piercing with a spear, stick, arrow, or similar objects from many other causes.
But wounds that occur in different parts of the body, such as a wound on the head, neck, chest, abdomen, groin, and similar areas on other limbs.
I am only recommending the treatment for some wounds as a guideline for treating other wounds.
I will begin with simple wounds of the head, as the memory of compound wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it was caused by striking with a stone or something similar, and the skull has only been cracked slightly and is a large wound, and you fear that an abscess may form in it, then you should quickly perform a venesection (phlebotomy) on the cephalic vein, and do not delay. And extract blood from the patient according to their vitality, but no more than necessary, especially if the blood that has come out of the wound is scanty.
And the venesection should be on the opposite side of the wound, and care must be taken to avoid overfilling (repletion), eating and drinking alcohol or heavy foods for the patient.
But if there is any reason for caution due to the patient's weak condition, then their diet should be reduced and they should avoid eating meat or drinking alcohol.
And place a compress on the wound, if it happens to be an abscess, make a plaster infused with roasted oil or vinegar in which has been steeped a styptic.
But if you are sure that the abscess has come to a head, then place a compress on the wound, if it is fresh and the discharge is still bloody, and sprinkle a little of the recommended powder on it once the air has not changed.
And if the air has already changed, then apply some ointment until it is healed.
But if the wound is large or deep due to a penetrating injury, and the lips of it are not properly approximated by pus, then approximate them with sutures as I have recommended in my instructions on suturing.
But if the wound has exposed bone and tendon, and is not retaining them but rather just a small piece of tissue, then cut it out and cure the wound with medicines and restore the flesh in place of that which is missing, and instruct the patient to abstain from foods that cause gas such as beans, cabbage, and similar foods until it has healed.
And if you find necrotic tissue in the wound that is not adhering to the bone, then cut it all out and remove it, and then cure the wound.
But if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood can flow and it has not been cut by medicines, then search for the artery and if you find it uncut, then cut it with a scalpel or tie it off; and if the situation requires that what I have said does not work, then cauterize it until the blood flow is stopped.
And if these wounds are simple and small, then the cause of them is light, in which case you should powder over them this powder before the air changes, so that it consolidates before the air changes.
And the method of the powder is as follows: take one part oil of lilies, two parts dragon's blood, and three parts unburnt alum; grind all of it to a very fine powder, and fill the wound with it, then constrict it well with a bandage until it adheres to it, and allow it to be coagulated by the blood.
And then strengthen it above with bandages and leave it alone, do not unbind it while it is not yet abscessed, because the medicine is not rendered ineffective until it has healed.
And sometimes do this alone with just oil of lilies when you do not have rose oil and dragon's blood available.
And perform this method of operation on large wounds when it is appropriate to place it over them and have them be tight, and on fresh wounds with their own blood that the air has not yet altered.
And if the air has altered them, especially in summertime, then do not attempt to use this powder, but rather cure them with what I have said, that is to say apply suitable ointments to them or place a poultice of barley flour with water and honey until it becomes putrid; and then cure them with the other treatment until they are healed.
But if a fracture occurs in the bone and it is small, then extract it with gentle force.
I say the cure for fractures of the skull is what is deadly poisonous.
Of wounds to the neck.
But if the wound occurs on the neck, then it is not different in treatment, and is similar to a simple wound of the head.
But if the nerves or artery of the neck are cut, then if it is nerves, do not apply treatment that causes strong stypticity to them, such as zinc and copper which are verdigris and similar things because it will cause damage to the nerves and contract them. And do not place any cause on the wound that is cold, because the substance of nerves is cold and its connection is with the brain, which is the source of all members.
And if it is treated with light medicines, such as washing the wound with warm water, sometimes infused in roasted or unroasted oil, and turpentine when it is washed with warm water and other similar remedies, and warm ointments.
But if the wound is large, then administer sutures or bring together the edges of it, and then cure it with bandages until it is healed.
But if the wound is deep or there is putrid matter in the lower part of it, then pierce it in the most depressed location.
But if an artery has been cut in the wound and blood flow has occurred, then separate or dry it out, or tie it off, or cauterize it if necessary.
But if the vertebrae of the neck have been cut and are saved, and the veins of the neck are intact, then bring together the edges of the wound with sutures on the ridge of the spine and do not touch it; lift it evenly and return it to its natural shape, and strengthen it with a suitable support, and leave it alone for several days; and then cure it with ointments that have stypticity and stimulation until it is healed.
But if the wound has damaged the bone, then percuss it, and if there are fragments of bone in it, remove all that you can; and what is not removable, leave it alone until the wound heals and becomes less painful, and allow it to separate and the pressure on it is relieved.

If the wound is caused by a lance or knife, and its depth is visible, then consider whether the wound is emitting foul-smelling breath; if so, know that the wound is deadly.
And if the wound is not deep and it is fresh with its own blood, then you should place powder on it in the first hour, but do not press hard to prevent the blood from being retained in the depth of the wound and returning to the heart and making the patient worse. Instead, put a attractive ointment on it and loosen the two veins twice a day.
And if the ointment is not available, then you should cover the opening of the wound with wool to absorb any discharge from the humors; and make sure that the patient rests on the wound so that any accumulated fluid in it can drain out.
But if three days or more have passed since the wound and the patient has not experienced convulsions, tremors of the heart, fainting spells, or other bad signs, then know that the wound is healing; and in that case, treat it with cupping glasses and other remedies until it is healed.
But if healing is delayed and the wound remains open at all times, then know that a fistula has formed; treat it with the method described in its own chapter.
If the wound is caused by a sword or knife and is simple on the surface of the arm or back, then treat it with stitches if it is large, or with powder if it is small.
But if pus has already formed in the bone and you see that it is coming out of it, then turn the wound and try to extract those pieces, if they are separate (from the bone). But if they are not separate, then leave them alone and allow the wound to heal, as extracting them will be easier once it has healed.
And for other wounds that occur on other parts of the body, the treatment in healing is the same as what has been said (before).
On wounds of the abdomen.
The indisposition that occurs in the abdomen is either great, small, or moderate.
A small disruption is made difficult to correct in any other way; and I know that returning the protrusion to its proper place is more difficult if you do not attend to it immediately, as it quickly swells and becomes engorged, making it difficult to return it to its proper location.
And therefore a moderate disruption is the best, as it is not difficult to return the intestine to its proper place in this case, unlike the two previous types of disruptions that are more difficult to correct.
And know that there are four ways to suture the abdomen, but two of them are common and similar to the suturing methods used for other wounds on the body.
And two other types of sutures are specific to abdominal wounds, but they are still used in the suturing of other wounds on the body as well.
I recommend that you learn each one with its explanation and description.
I say that when the wound is small and some part of the intestine protrudes from it, making it difficult to return it to its proper place, then it is in one of two conditions: either the disruption is small, as previously mentioned, or the intestine has become inflamed due to the coldness of the air.
And therefore when this is the case, it is necessary to make an incision in that part and submerge a sponge or cloth soaked in warm water alone, or in a mixture of wine, cinquefoil, and pepper, and insert it into the intestine until the inflammation subsides.
And sometimes it is necessary to use a styptic in this process, as warm water alone may not be sufficient to resolve the inflammation.
And once you have seen that the inflammation has subsided, then you should moisten the intestine with water that contains mallow and marshmallow, as this will alleviate the difficulty of returning it to its proper place with minimal effort.
But if it is not necessary to return the intestine to its proper place, then you should make an incision along the disruption using a small instrument suitable for cutting hemorrhoids.
And the primary treatment is best when it involves making an incision that does not extend too deep and does not cause unnecessary bleeding or weakening of the area.
Regarding the instrument, know its shape:
The instrument has one curved and sharp end, and the other end is not sharp; its tip should be fine but not as thin as a spatula, and it should be slightly blunt at the end.
And therefore when the wound is large and part of the intestine protrudes from it, then it is necessary to return it to its proper place in its natural shape, if possible in its original location, as this is best.
But when the disruption is large and located in the lower part of the abdomen, then it is necessary for the patient to lie on their back with their hips raised higher than their head; and if it is located in the upper part of the abdomen, then you should place the patient's head and chest higher than their hips.
And similarly, if the disruption is on either side of the abdomen, then you should always keep your attention and focus on that side so that the higher part of the abdomen can be used to return the intestine to its proper place.
And it is also necessary to use this method for both large and moderate wounds.
And for small wounds, use whatever method you have prepared and make sure that the person assisting you holds the disruption open with their hand while adjusting its lips, revealing any other area that may require suturing.
This is the common method of suturing: take a needle or a threaded needle according to the size of the wound; then place it at the edge of the disruption on your ring finger and tighten the needle once without piercing both ends of the thread with the needle, so that you can insert the two ends of the thread into the inner parts of the wound. Then you have connected the two ends of the thread to the two ends of the needle, and this has been done four times. [Note: There is a mistake in the original text, as it says "entro que fassas aquela penetrar de aquela partida" which means "until you make it penetrate that part", but it should say "entro que fassas aquela penetrar en aquella partida" which means "until you make it penetrate into that part".]
And then tighten the needle with double thread, and sometimes two parts at once, and then bring together the lips of the wound with proper alignment; and then leave space for your finger and insert another needle into it, and tie that needle with thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this with the needles until you have completed suturing the entire wound.
And the needles should be of moderate thickness between fine and thick, as very thin needles easily cut through the flesh and very thick ones are difficult to insert into the thread, so it is necessary for them to be moderate in terms of fineness and thickness.
And it is not necessary for the needle to be inserted too deeply into both ends of the thread, as this may cause the flesh to be cut slightly and the wound to open up before it has healed properly.
And do not use prolonged stitches in suturing, as this may prevent the wound from healing properly.
And then blunt the ends of the needles so that they do not poke the patient while they sleep, and place powder around the sutures on all sides to keep the needle ends in place; leave them there until you are sure that the wound has healed properly.
And this type of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as it only requires one or two stitches or around that amount.
The second common method of suturing is to use a threaded needle to connect all four ends (the two ends of the thread and the two ends of the wound) in one go, with a needle that has fine and thick thread wrapped around it.
And when you have penetrated these four ends with the needle, return it to its starting point by withdrawing it from that deeper part of the wound, causing the thread to retract and rise up to the surface of the wound, similar to how fabric is sewn together with a stitch that holds it in place.
And leave a space between each stitch equal to the width of your smallest finger.
This method is common among men.
I used this method to suture a wound on a man's abdomen, which he had received from being stabbed with a knife; the disruption of the wound was larger than a palm in size, and part of the intestines had protruded about two palms' width from the middle location of the intestine; the disruption was located in the middle of the abdomen. I returned his intestines to their proper place after they had been outside the wound for twenty-four hours.
The wound healed within fifteen days or so, and I cured him and he recovered; and as far as I know, he lived for many years and continued to live his life in good health.
And other doctors had judged that he would not recover; it was a miracle that I cured him without using ointment, as there was no ointment or any medicine available in that location, but I applied clean cloths to the wound twice a day and bathed it regularly with honey water until it healed.
But I will now describe two other types of suturing, as told in the book "Paraula".
The first type involves starting with the thread and inserting the needle from the outer part of the wound to the inner part.
And when the needle penetrates into the thread and into the deeper layer of flesh in a straight line and to the full length of the body, leave the end of the thread attached to the needle; then insert the needle from the inner part of the wound to the outer part at the other end of the incision. And when you have inserted the needle in this manner, then insert it again into the same outer end of the incision, going from the outer part to the inner part; leave the end of the thread that is on this side and insert the needle into the other end of the deeper layer, going from the inner part to the outer part. And then insert the needle again in the same manner, going from the outer part to the inner part of the wound, until it fully penetrates into the deeper layer. And then start from this same side and suture the outer end of the thread to the inner end on the other side, withdrawing the needle that was inserted; return it to its original position in the thread and suture the outer end of the thread to the inner end on the other side using the other needle. But the second type of suturing, which I just now called "Galician," is as its name suggests and is done in this way: you sew that seam with the ligament, in such a way that the medicines heal that, connecting all parts to their corresponding part, naturally; and they apply one end of it and the other end of it to the other end of it, and this is done as I have told you.
It is necessary that you insert the needle in the outside end of the wound, at your own side, and make it penetrate into the inside part of it in the same hole, and leave two ends of the ligament; and then turn the needle around and make it penetrate from the outside to the inside in the other two ends of the ligament.
And then turn those knots and make each of them penetrate from the inside to the outside in the other two ends of the wound that are on the opposite side.

Varicose veins are a type of vascular lesion characterized by dilated, tortuous, and swollen veins, usually in the legs. They can be caused by various factors such as aging, pregnancy, obesity, prolonged standing, or genetic predisposition.
Varices are varicose veins, which are large and swollen veins filled with melancholic superfluities that appear in several parts of the body, but most commonly in the legs, especially among travelers, workers, and carriers.

On the incision of worms generated under the skin, called "bovine disease".
This illness is called "bovine disease" in some lands because it often affects cattle and is a worm that is born between the kidney and the flesh, and it travels through the whole body going up and down, and it is noticeable by its movement from one part of the body to another until it breaks the kidney and emerges.
And its generation is due to the putrefaction of some humors, just like the worms and snakes and earthworms and ascariasis that are generated in the belly.

On the incision of "nafir" disease.
This illness is called "nafir" in our land, it is pain which appears in some members and moves from one member to another.
I have seen that as I will tell you. I was called to a sick woman in a village, and I uncovered her arm and saw a small inflammation on the saphenous vein of the arm, and after an hour had passed, I saw that inflammation move like a worm crawling upwards, but more slowly than it would be if it were alive, similar to silver flowing from place to place.
And then the pain moves to that place and settles in the muscle, and therefore stay here for an hour.
And then heal the other body until it reaches the other arm.
And then he told me to turn around and let him examine my whole body as he saw fit; it was quite remarkable the transformation in him and the speed with which he moved from one member to the next. And I had already seen before in my own heels in that manner, but I have also seen many [people] who experience pain being transferred from one member to another. But I did not see that with the heels in the same way as in the woman.
And I did not think it was that, but rather because the woman was old, and had dry skin and visible veins, and in this case it appeared to be the sensation of gas being transferred.
And it is necessary that this reverse treatment not appear in those who are delicate and have warm bodies with narrow veins.
And when you want to treat the patient and they feel the pain, then do not appear to them as we have said, but rather strengthen yourself over that area and lightly press down on it, and cauterize the spot where the trapped gas is released.
But if you do not see it with your own eyes, then treat it with a laxative of the body and with that which expels gas, and singe those areas with stinking pills and Serapian pills and similar ones.
On the extraction of arrows.
Arrows are diverse in terms of their species and the locations on the body where they become lodged, for their diversity consists of those with large tips, small ones, concave ones, blunt ones, and sharp ones; and of those with three points, and those that have tongues; and of those that have feathers.
And of the signs of death is when an arrow catches in it and passes through bone, and exits the skull which is above the brain, for this causes sudden violence, loss of vision, vertigo, numbness in the feet, inflammation and numbness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of thought, vomiting of bile, and quickly the voice becomes hoarse and words are difficult to articulate, and white fluid like dust is emitted from the wound, and there is a similar discharge of liquid from the flesh.
And therefore if you see these signs, then you should refrain from treating or extracting the arrow, unless it is necessary to do so.
But the signs of an arrow that catches in the heart, when it is close to the left breast, and feels as if it is embedded in a hard cause, and is not visible; and quickly the movement of the arrow resembles the pulse, and there is dark blood flowing from the wound, and the extremities become cold, and there is chills and fainting; and therefore know that death approaches swiftly.
And the signs when an arrow has wounded a lung are foamy blood flowing from the wound, and swelling near the neck, and the patient's complexion changes, and they exhale great amounts of air and ask for fresh air to be brought.
And if an arrow catches in the fascia that is in the feet, then the pain becomes located near the small ribs, and a great and intense pain occurs with deep breathing and sighing, and not all of the limbs' muscles are affected.
And if an arrow catches in the stomach, then quickly there is discharge from the wound of undigested food.
And if an arrow catches in the belly and is embedded in it, there will be a tear or rent in the wound or membrane or intestine that has been ruptured, and there is no hope for the cure of the patient through the extraction of the arrow.
And if the arrow catches in the bladder and urine flows from it, and there is some cause that comes out of it externally, and quickly there is pain over the patient, then know that it is fatal.
But the other members such as the face, neck, and shoulders, the shoulder blades, the vertebrae of the back, the collarbone, the hip, the thigh, and similar parts of the limbs are saved according to the greater circumstances when the arrow does not strike a vein or artery and is not poisonous.

Stopping bleeding can be challenging in some situations due to the small size of the wound and the possibility of swelling in the arm. In such cases, you may need to apply pressure on the area for a longer period or use a tourniquet to restrict blood flow to the affected limb. It is important to closely monitor the patient's condition and ensure that bleeding has stopped completely before releasing the tourniquet. Of ventosation (or bloodletting through cupping) and the qualities of its use.
Ventosations (or bloodletting through cupping) are used for corns, or for erysipelas (inflammation of the skin), or for abscesses.
Ventosation (or bloodletting through cupping) is performed in two ways: one method involves making an incision and extracting blood, while the other method involves ventosation without making an incision.
And this method of ventosation (or bloodletting through cupping) that is without incision is performed in two ways: either with fire or without fire.
And the locations on the body where bloodletting through cupping with incision and extraction of blood are administered are fourteen in number, of which one is placed on the nape of the neck, and is called alnocrati; and another is at the back of the head, at the base of the skull; and bloodletting on the mandible below the jawbone, behind the mouth; and bloodletting with two spatulas; and bloodletting in the armpit, above the elbow; and bloodletting in the groin, at the top of the thigh; and bloodletting in two places, one on each calf; and bloodletting in two places, one on each knee.
And ventosation does not extract blood from the small veins spread throughout the flesh, but rather through them, and for this reason it does not diminish their virtue as is commonly done with phlebotomy; nor is it necessary that ventosation be performed with or without fire in any illness caused by repletion until the entire body has been evacuated.
But if there is a need for ventosation due to illness or chronic conditions, administer it at any time during the beginning and end of each month, in the middle of the day and night, and at regular intervals.
And therefore, when you see any of these causes, and particularly during the third or middle part of the month, then we command that ventosation be performed more than two or three hours after passing midday.

Chapter one.
Summaries and collections on the nature of bone fractures, including those necessary premises before we begin the memory aid for each broken member and its various types. And so I say that when a fracture or dislocation or sprain or swelling occurs, it is necessary for you to begin with bloodletting or applying leeches, or both, if no reason prohibits it, such as weakness of strength, or if the person is an infant, very old and decrepit, or during a time of intense heat or cold.

And I will begin with a memory aid for each type of fracture, explained in its own separate chapter.
The diversity of fractures within itself. And the types of bone fractures are diverse; for there is one type of fracture that results in a bowing shape, and other times it occurs along the length of the bone. Furthermore, there are also fractures caused by splinters and fragments, both protruding and non-protruding, similar to how a wound appears when it's prepared to be written on. Additionally, there is a type of fracture with contusion and disruption in the skull, as well as a small fissure fracture.
And each type has its own particular challenge or difficulty in healing, according to the distinct memory that will come from its location.
Sign(s) of bone fracture. And so a bone fracture is recognized by its deformity, as well as the prominence and sensation of it being apparent to touch, and also by how it feels when compressed with one's hand.
And therefore, when there is no apparent deformity or prominence and it does not feel that way when touched, nor does the patient experience significant pain when pressing on it with agitation, then it is not a bone fracture.
However, it is possible that there may be deformity or a small fissure, and in such cases, it is not necessary to manipulate it with one's hand or apply compression on the entire area. Instead, place a medicine over it that recalls the appropriate remedy for that location, and make it tight with subtle constriction.
And know that when the location is bowed but not split into two or has some other condition like swelling, as with the entire part being compared, then it is necessary to begin immediately with the rectification of it, which may require surgical incision and removal of pus.
And if there is surgical incision and removal of pus, then leave it for several days until the pus ceases to drain, and then dress it in any way that you can using lightness and gentleness.
And know that the healing process and swelling of it is easier than in a bone where there is a splintered fracture.
And make it strong according to how it recovers.
But if the bone is splintered, then it is necessary to extend the broken limb with two parts, whether it's an arm or a leg, or with one hand if the limb is small, or using two ropes or one rope and a hand.
And your position should be such that you place the limb in its natural shape while extending the broken parts, and then make sure to adjust those pieces with gentleness and in any way that you can in their locations.
And be cautious with your strength, ensuring that you do not cause pain or injury to the patient through your operation, and make sure to use your skills to align each bone with its companion in the best possible way.
And it is essential that you touch the affected area with your hand at that time, and if there are any other reasons for deviation, correct it and adjust it according to the degree of your strength.

And it is necessary that the threads be medium in thickness and fineness, and be of linen; and if the threads are thick, as I have seen with some foolish doctors using heavy ropes made of twisted linen, this is a great error because it prevents equal tension.
And also fine threads are not appropriate because you will not be able to obtain the desired tension with them, and it is not appropriate for there to be less than a finger-width between star and star.
